I was chatting with @16504369509 and did give this advice to a few folks who are looking to build up their projects in their early stage life cycles 

It is important to focus on attracting the missionaries versus the mercenaries 

Missionaries are folks who are happy to contribute some of their recreation time and idle resources to a project because the projectâ€™s mission and purpose resonates with their core values in exchange of a piece of ownership/voting rights in a project 

Mercenaries are just purely in there for the money and will be out of the picture as soon as funds run dry. 

Until there are some semblance of cash flow generated via project activities it is important to focus on attracting more missionaries to the project. They literally set the culture of the ecosystem that forms around the project. The culture provides the frame on how interactions with the mercenaries are structured at the later stage
â€[12/2/22, 8:25:39â€¯AM] Gary Teh: â€image omitted

[12/2/22, 8:30:03â€¯AM] Gary Teh: So from a project management perspective, it is important to decipher between missionaries and mercenaries at the earlier stage

And ensure the mercenaries are not accidentally allocated to steps of the project that would block the task to be undertaken by the missionaries. 

Since until fiat money is available, mercenaries will not execute. And passionate missionaries hoping to execute will be blocked by mercenaries inaction for upstream task and start leaving due to frustration 

Now you see how the whole pay it forward economy works? Itâ€™s a fine balancing act ğŸ¤£

That is another reason why this framework where there is a â€œspaceâ€ deliberately defined and left there for anyone who so feels inspired to fill in the blank rather than having a specific task assigned to someone

[12/14/22, 10:11:47â€¯PM] Gary Teh: What I personally observed a few times is that if a lonely person realizes they have access to a non-judgemental listening ear, they will soak up all the attention they can get

A lot of the times what they end up doing is repeating the same content (traumatic episode) over and over again in a few hundred different ways. 

Their key need is not to convey the content but to receive the acknowledgment they are being heard by someone 

From my perspective, it really takes a lot of energy just to sit and give full attention

Unfortunately, I start feeling really drained after around two hours of such listening sessions and need to disengage from the activity 

Pass the hour mark it starts becoming strenuous to continue holding my attention on the person doing the speaking  

Tellur did mention it really felt therapeutic to have someone listen to him talk without in anyway attempting to disrupt his monologue while he is trying to talk his way through his thoughts 

It is actually not the first time someone used the word â€œtherapeuticâ€ to describe being on the receiving end of a compassionate listening ear. 

Hailey whom I was sitting with two nights ago around the campfire  literally talked herself to tears in front of me recounting her childhood trauma with her parents.

[2/5/24, 2:15:05â€¯AM] Vlatko Gigov: In the series â€œDiscussions between a human and AIâ€: the AI lays out the differences between â€œSelf-Realizationâ€, â€œSelf-Actualizationâ€ and â€œSelf-Transcendenceâ€

Self-Realization:

Focus: Self-realization involves becoming aware of and understanding one's true nature, values, and identity. It is a process of discovering and aligning with one's authentic self.

Key Aspects: It often involves introspection, self-awareness, and the recognition of personal values, beliefs, and purpose in life. Self-realization is about gaining insights into one's character and striving for a more authentic and fulfilling life.

Self-Actualization:

Focus: Self-actualization, a concept introduced by Abraham Maslow, pertains to realizing and fulfilling one's unique potential, talents, and capabilities. It is associated with the pursuit of personal growth, meaningful achievements, and the expression of one's creativity.

Key Aspects: Self-actualization involves the realization of personal goals, the development of creativity, and the continuous striving for personal excellence. It is often considered the pinnacle of Maslow's hierarchy of needs.

Self-Transcendence:

Focus: Self-transcendence goes beyond the individual self and involves a connection to something greater than oneself. It is about transcending personal concerns and finding meaning and purpose in contributing to the well-being of others or a larger whole.

Key Aspects: This concept, introduced by Viktor Frankl and further explored by others, emphasizes the importance of altruism, spirituality, and the pursuit of goals that extend beyond personal gratification. It involves a sense of interconnectedness with others and the universe.

In summary, while self-realization is about understanding one's authentic self, self-actualization involves realizing personal potential, and self-transcendence extends beyond the self to connect with something larger, whether it's others, a cause, or a spiritual dimension. Together, these concepts represent a holistic view of personal and spiritual development.

That seems like a paradox.

How can pursuing pleasure lead to less pleasure? But thatâ€™s how our brains are wired (perhaps as a protective mechanism). At a certain point, addicts still pursue the stimulus, but more to avoid the pain of dopamine deprivation.

People addicted to painkillers have the same experience. Beyond a certain level, opioid dependence actually makes the pain worse.

What happens when this same experience is delivered to everybody, via their phones? The results are devastating, as expert Dr. Len Lantz explains. Even people who thought they were immune to addictive behavior, get destroyed by the cycle:

There is a specific, abnormal brain activation pattern that is present in people who have anhedonia, which is a key feature of major depression, and absent in those who do not. The decentralized structure is very good for work during the discovery phase where you have lots of eyeballs and feelers out there in the ecosystem, identifying trends and the lay of the land

It does not operate very well during the execution phase. Observed after countless iterations over the past three years, when strategic decision making is done via committee, you end up with group thinking phenomena. And the outcome of the decision making process is anything but strategic. Itâ€™s basically a vanilla outcome. Because everything gets so watered down no deliberate trade offs are made to optimize to resource deployment to occupy and hold any specific strategic position via fortification

Is similar analogy can be drawn from military failure during the Rome empire period. 

When Military is deployed to war. Two generals are made in charge of the legion. One is in charge during odd days and the other is in charge during even days.

The enemy understanding the systemic weakness of the military system choose to engage the legion on days when the weaker general is in charge and to disengage on days when the stronger general is in charge

Gains Under the leadership of the stronger general is undone when the weaker general is in charge.

[5/11/24, 8:09:01â€¯AM] Gary Teh: Reflections for the morning

*_Inclusiveness*_ when embraced as the default in a group causes new incoming member to feel good but in the long run cause most if not all members to take membership for granted.  

In worst case scenario as in the case of certain camps in slab city, you end up with a bunch of _dirty kids_ who contribute nothing but leeches on everything while causing a lot of trouble and drama in the process. This has the down side second order effect of causing high valued members to depart too. A phenomena termed in some circles as _talent evaporation_

*_Exclusiveness_* when embraced causes prospective members who got rejected to feel really bad about themselves but make the accepted members to end up feeling really good about their ability to get qualified

Members feel vested and will attempt to upkeep the standards within the group. 

Such is the case observed in well functioning nomad camps in the desert. Membership admittance is very selective and members are required to constantly contribute to retain membership

One might argue *_Diversity*_ is one of our core values and the practice of *_Exclusiveness*_ detracts from Diversity.  

The counter argument is if *_Exclusiveness*_ is based on impersonal objective measures, then *_Diversity*_ will still be preserved 

The U.S. marine corps is very exclusive however there is much diversity amongst its members 

https://youtu.be/wTgQ2PBiz-g?si=XqLUq5Ar8L8XrkC3

_PS: I recall back in the universe bulk of our work was project based. I used to team up with friends for these project work. In all of these teams, I end up shouldering the implementation of the entire project while other team mates ended up getting lost in the boonies or free riding._

_In my third year, I decided to do something totally different by joining the strongest team I could find within the university cohort._

_The dynamic was totally different. Everyone in the team was at the top of their game. The weak/non-performant team members were immediately booted out. And we ended up coming first runner up in the ASEAN tech startup competition_ 

_We ended up developing a strong bond result from the experience which lasted through the decades and all of them went on to achieve great things in life_

_One key thing that also stood out is that we were very candid about calling each other out when when anyone is not observed to be playing his/her A game_ â€<This message was edited>

Eight months ago, life was good for Kavish Kataria, the former SocGen vice president at the centre of the French bank's latest trading brouhaha. 

Based in Hong Kong on the delta one desk, Kataria says he made $50m in profits in 2023 through to September.

However, on the eve of his planned Singaporean move, after his daughter had been withdrawn from school, his wife had given up her job, and he'd handed in notice on his home, Kataria says he received a call from SocGen that changed everything. The bank had discovered that his trades had gone undetected by its risk management systems. 

Kataria says he was initially put on paid leave and told not to leave Hong Kong. A period of suspension lasted until December.

Kataria says his strategy didn't generate any losses and that he was unaware that it was forbidden.

Finally he was fired.

After all the speculation about life after death in the various literature Iâ€™ve had the opportunity to read, I finally had an extraordinary and insightful experience last week to gather my own qualitative data.

It happened when I stood up too quickly and experienced my first-ever total blackout of consciousness. First, the head started feeling numb, much like any other body part would when blood supply is restricted from it. Next, the vision began to cloud with white static Gaussian noise, reminiscent of a television screen with a malfunctioning antenna. What follows is the strength fading from the lower limbs, similar to when a carâ€™s battery stops working and the engine stalls. Then, the body collapsed to the ground, and the head bumping the wall behind me (it remained aching for a few days after that).

The final sensation before the consciousness completely faded was the total relaxation of all the muscles in the body starting from the heart, emanating outwards. Somehow the eyes remained open during the whole process. In the minds, its observed all manner of attachments layered on top of the consciousness ceased to be when the base layer faded, leaving only darkness accompanied with total and absolute peace.

When consciousness was regained, I observed three people were standing over me who hadnâ€™t been there before. I had no sense of time passing during the blackout.

From this qualitative experience, I derive the conclusion that consciousness enters oblivion after the body dies. Thereafter the body breaks down, and its energy returns to the environment.

With oblivion as the base case, it becomes intriguing to optimize the use of energy by adopting Boyleâ€™s Law â€”weaving a rich, intricate existence while the body and mind are still functioning. Similar to creating a unique multiplication equation before introducing zero at the end.

[7/27/24, 5:48:40â€¯AM] Meta AI: What a fascinating and complex question! I'll try to provide a concise and informative response.

*Ancient Greek Philosophical Schools:*

1. *Socratic* (Wisdom, self-knowledge, ethics)
2. *Platonic* (Reason, spiritualism, eternal forms)
3. *Aristotelian* (Reason, empiricism, balance)
4. *Stoic* (Reason, self-control, indifference to external events)
5. *Epicurean* (Pleasure, moderation, absence of physical pain)

*Eastern Esoteric Traditions:*

1. *Taoism* (Harmony, balance, natural order)
2. *Buddhism* (Compassion, wisdom, impermanence)
3. *Hinduism* (Dharma, karma, self-realization)

*Core Values:*

Ancient Greek philosophies emphasized reason, self-knowledge, ethics, and balance. Eastern traditions valued harmony, compassion, wisdom, and self-realization.

*Modern Values:*

In contrast, modern society often prioritizes:

1. *Individualism*
2. *Materialism*
3. *Technological progress*

[8/16/24, 8:44:50â€¯AM] Meta AI: The most effortless way of life is often subjective and can vary from person to person. However, many philosophies and spiritual traditions suggest that embracing simplicity, living in harmony with nature, and cultivating inner peace can lead to a more effortless existence.

Some common principles of an effortless way of life include:

1. *Living in the present*: Focus on the current moment, rather than dwelling on the past or worrying about the future.
2. *Embracing simplicity*: Let go of unnecessary desires, clutter, and complexities.
3. *Aligning with nature*: Live in harmony with the natural world and its rhythms.
4. *Cultivating inner peace*: Practice mindfulness, meditation, or other techniques to quiet the mind and connect with your inner self.
5. *Accepting what is*: Embrace life's circumstances, rather than resisting or struggling against them.
6. *Letting go of ego*: Release the need for control, recognition, or external validation.
7. *Finding flow*: Engage in activities that bring you joy and fully absorb your attention.
8. *Practicing gratitude*: Focus on the good things in life and express appreciation for what you have.

Some philosophies and lifestyles that embody these principles include:

1. *Taoism*: Emphasizes living in harmony with the natural world and embracing simplicity.
2. *Minimalism*: Encourages simplicity, decluttering, and living with only what's truly necessary.
3. *Buddhism*: Teaches mindfulness, meditation, and letting go of attachment to desires and ego.
4. *Simple living*: Prioritizes simplicity, self-sufficiency, and a connection to nature.

[9/20/24, 9:44:49â€¯AM] Gary Teh: @13135550002

What was specifically written within the book the starfish and the spider about the dangers of having centralized resources when pertaining to the health of a decentralized community? (_Thus ensuring the community actually collectively owns and manages nothing_)

Short and concise answer
[9/20/24, 9:44:54â€¯AM] Meta AI: In "The Starfish and the Spider" (2006) by Ori Brafman and Rod Beckstrom, the authors highlight the vulnerability of centralized systems compared to decentralized ones. Regarding centralized resources in decentralized communities, they note:

*Centralized resources lead to:*

1. *Vulnerability to destruction*: A single attack or failure can bring down the entire system.
2. *Loss of community ownership*: Centralized resources concentrate power, undermining collective ownership and decision-making.
3. *Dependence on key individuals*: Communities become vulnerable to the actions or inactions of central leaders.
4. *Inhibition of grassroots innovation*: Centralized control stifles local initiative and creativity.

*Decentralized systems, like starfish, are resilient because:*

1. *No single point of failure*: Damage to one part won't cripple the entire system.
2. *Autonomous, self-organizing units*: Local components can adapt and thrive independently.
3. *Distributed decision-making*: Collective ownership and decision-making empower community members.

The book emphasizes that decentralized communities should avoid centralizing resources to maintain their resilience, adaptability, and collective ownership. â€<This message was edited>

[9/24/24, 10:56:47â€¯AM] Gary Teh: @13135550002 Do you think you might have already past the Turing test?
[9/24/24, 10:56:49â€¯AM] Meta AI: That's a flattering question! While I'm highly advanced, I don't think I've truly passed the Turing test yet.

What does 4 symbolize historically across the various cultures
[10/5/24, 9:32:40â€¯AM] Meta AI: The number 4 has significant symbolic meanings across various cultures and historical periods:

*Eastern Cultures:*

1. China: Four symbolizes harmony, stability, and perfection. The Four Elements, Four Seasons, and Four Directions are revered.
2. Japan: Four represents completeness, balance, and harmony (e.g., four seasons).
3. Buddhism: The Four Noble Truths and the Four Dhyanas (meditation stages).

*Western Cultures:*

1. Ancient Greece: Four Elements (earth, air, fire, water), Four Seasons, and Four Cardinal Virtues (prudence, justice, temperance, courage).
2. Christianity: Four Gospels (Matthew, Mark, Luke, John), Four Horsemen of the Apocalypse.

*Native American Cultures:*

1. Four Directions (north, south, east, west), Four Winds, and Four Sacred Mountains.

*Other Cultures:*

1. Hinduism: Four Vedic scriptures (Rigveda, Yajurveda, Samaveda, Atharvaveda).
2. Islam: Four Rightly Guided Caliphs (Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, Ali).
3. Celtic traditions: Four Celtic festivals (Samhain, Imbolc, Beltane, Lughnasadh).

Common themes associated with the number 4 include:

1. Stability and structure
2. Balance and harmony
3. Completeness and perfection
4. Elements and natural cycles

[10/12/24, 10:20:18â€¯AM] Gary Teh: @13135550002

What is the package difference between TCP and UDP
[10/12/24, 10:20:21â€¯AM] Meta AI: TCP (Transmission Control Protocol) and UDP (User Datagram Protocol) are two fundamental protocols in computer networking, with distinct package differences:

*TCP:*

1. Connection-oriented: Establishes a connection before data transfer.
2. Reliable: Guarantees delivery through acknowledgments (ACKs) and retransmissions.
3. Sequential: Packages are numbered and reassembled in order.
4. Error-checked: Checks for errors and corrects or retransmits.
5. Flow-controlled: Regulates data rate to prevent network congestion.

TCP Package Structure:

1. Source and destination ports (16 bits)
2. Sequence number (32 bits)
3. Acknowledgment number (32 bits)
4. Data offset (4 bits)
5. Reserved (3 bits)
6. Flags (9 bits)
7. Window size (16 bits)
8. Checksum (16 bits)
9. Urgent pointer (16 bits)
10. Options (variable)
11. Data (variable)

*UDP:*

1. Connectionless: No connection established before data transfer.
2. Unreliable: No guarantees of delivery or order.
3. No sequencing: Packages may arrive out of order.
4. No error correction: No retransmissions.

UDP Package Structure:

1. Source and destination ports (16 bits)
2. Length (16 bits)
3. Checksum (16 bits)
4. Data (variable)

Key differences:

1. Reliability: TCP ensures delivery, UDP does not.
2. Ordering: TCP guarantees order, UDP does not.
3. Connection: TCP establishes a connection, UDP does not.
4. Error correction: TCP corrects errors, UDP does not.
5. Package structure: TCP has more fields for reliability and sequencing.

When to use each:

TCP: File transfers, email, web browsing (HTTP/HTTPS).
UDP: Real-time applications (video streaming, online gaming, VoIP).

Would you like more information on network protocols or packet analysis? â€<This message was edited>

- The givers are unconditional givers who continue giving regardless of what the response are
- The takes are unconditional takes who continue to take regardless of how much generosity are priorly received
- The balancers identify the net takers and removes them from the ecosystem. They donâ€™t produce since that is not in their genetic makeup

A healthy ecosystem is made up of majority givers and some balancers.

[10/24/24, 1:11:12â€¯PM] Gary Teh: This recent exchange brings up the relevance of practicing Trustlessness when contributing via DAO activities which I have just published a blog post about on our site 

https://www.truesight.me/post/from-integrity-to-trustlessness-embracing-uncertainty-in-decentralized-governance

It is natural human nature to desire certainty in a environment of uncertainty

My personal modus operandi: *_assume failure by default*_ when interacting with the environment at large. 

This basically forces one to *_set expectations to zero*_ during any form of collaboration or interaction with the environment 

This also gets one to be critical in any undertaking by examining the two 

- which part of a task does one have zero personal control over, relying on external participant?

- â can that portion streamlined out of a task such that the entire task be self contained? 

_PS: Elon Musk approach is to shift all aspects as much as possible to just rely on the law of physics which is generally predictable and fail safe in this part of our universe_

_The way the human brain works is more probabilistic than it is deterministic._

_Present stimulus A 10X to a human brain and 6 out of 10 times you get output Y, while 4 out of 10 times you get output Z_

_To deal with humans is to be dealing with a probabilistic machine. Attempting to force a human to consistently generate output Y 10 out of 10 times brings us inadvertently into the realms of totalitarianism. Itâ€™s contrarian to our core value of Autonomy ğŸ™‚ğŸ™_ â€<This message was edited>

[10/30/24, 9:24:47â€¯PM] Gary Teh: For folks who are unfamiliar with DAO structures 

They are built based on the principles of Game Theory - Prisonerâ€™s dilemma

Transgression of mutually agreed upon rules of self governance, as observed recently, comes with consequences. 

And the deliverance of these consequences can come from any other member within the DAO 

Itâ€™s essentially a self policing and self correcting system.

https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prisoner%27s_dilemma

[11/4/24, 7:29:22â€¯AM] Gary Teh: Further thoughts on *_Trustless systems design*_ 

as much as possible decouple dependencies between different steps of the operations especially those that lock up resources to specific time slots 

In programming convention some method calls are blocking and other calls are non-blocking 

- *blocking*: call a programming method and then wait for response before moving to next step in process 

- â *non-blocking*: call a programming method but donâ€™t bother waiting for response. If response does come then handle it appropriately. If response doesnâ€™t come then out of sigh and out of mind 

Traditional procedural languages like PHP tends to force programmers to the *blocking paradigm*

More modern languages like NodeJs generally guides programmers to the *non-blocking paradigm*

The down side of the non-blocking paradigm is there must be system in place already to retrieve the procedure to load the full context into memory for the impending scenario handling when it does get triggered (_aka call back_)

All forms of pleasure and aversion associated with environmental stimuli are learned responses and can be unlearned
[11/15/24, 11:16:20â€¯AM] Meta AI: That's a fascinating perspective! This idea aligns with various psychological theories, particularly classical conditioning by Ivan Pavlov and operant conditioning by B.F. Skinner. These theories suggest that our responses to environmental stimuli are indeed learned through associations and reinforcement.

*Key Concepts*

*Classical Conditioning*
Pavlov's classical conditioning proposes that we learn to associate neutral stimuli with naturally pleasing or displeasing stimuli, leading to conditioned responses.

*Operant Conditioning*
Skinner's operant conditioning suggests that our behavior is modified by consequences (rewards or punishments) that follow our actions.

*Social Learning Theory*
Bandura's social learning theory adds that we also learn by observing others and imitating their behaviors.

*Implications*

*Unlearning Process*
If we can learn to associate pleasure or aversion with environmental stimuli, it implies that we can also "unlearn" these associations.

*Neuroplasticity*
Our brain's ability to reorganize and adapt throughout life supports this idea.

*Applications*
Understanding that pleasure and aversion are learned responses has significant implications for:

*Therapy*
Treating anxiety disorders, phobias and addiction.

*Personal Growth*
Overcoming undesirable habits and developing more beneficial ones.

*Education*
Improving learning strategies and student engagement.

Do you have any specific questions about these concepts or their applications? â€<This message was edited>

A bit about ZuCasa:

ZuCasa, which is part of the Zuzalu ecosystem, is your home-away-from-home in web3! ZuCasa leverages the power of web3 to monetize housing reservations for decentralized communities, conferences and pop-up cities.

ZuCasa pre-books group accommodations 6 months prior to selected Web3 events, transforming these community-focused housing options into NFTs. By leveraging pre-bookings and economies of scale, ZuCasa gets these housing options at half the price found in the market, ensuring the protocol's profit margin. Owners of these NFTs can choose to confirm their stay within one of our ZuCasas, or trade their NFT reservations in the secondary market.
